<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)" title="American Idol (season 8)">American Idol (season 8)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kris_Allen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kris_Allen.jpg/170px-Kris_Allen.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kris_Allen.jpg/255px-Kris_Allen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Kris_Allen.jpg/340px-Kris_Allen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="472" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kris_Allen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_8)" title="American Idol (season 8)">eighth season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The eighth season premiered on January 13, 2009. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Darnell" title="Mike Darnell">Mike Darnell</a>, the president of alternative programming for Fox, stated that the season would focus more on the contestants' personal life.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first major change to the judging panel, a fourth judge, Kara DioGuardi, was introduced. This was also the first season without executive producer <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Lythgoe" title="Nigel Lythgoe">Nigel Lythgoe</a> who left to focus on the international versions of his show <i><a href="/wiki/So_You_Think_You_Can_Dance_(US)" class="mw-redirect" title="So You Think You Can Dance (US)">So You Think You Can Dance</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The Hollywood round was moved to the Kodak Theatre for 2009 and was also extended to two weeks. <i>Idol Gives Back</i> was canceled for this season due to the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">global recession</a> at the time.
</p><p>There were 13 finalists this season, but two were eliminated in the first result show of the finals. A new feature introduced was the "Judges' Save", and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Giraud" title="Matt Giraud">Matt Giraud</a> was saved from elimination at the top seven by the judges when he received the fewest votes. The next week, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Rounds" title="Lil Rounds">Lil Rounds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anoop_Desai" title="Anoop Desai">Anoop Desai</a> were eliminated.
</p><p>The two finalists were <a href="/wiki/Kris_Allen" title="Kris Allen">Kris Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a>, both of whom had previously landed in the bottom three at the top five. Allen won the contest in the most controversial voting result since the second season. It was claimed,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and then later retracted,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> that 38&#160;million of the 100&#160;million votes cast on the night came from Allen's home state of Arkansas alone, and that AT&amp;T employees unfairly influenced the votes by giving lessons on power-texting at viewing parties in Arkansas.<sup id="cite_ref-textgate_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-textgate-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Both Allen and Lambert released the coronation song, "<a href="/wiki/No_Boundaries_(song)" title="No Boundaries (song)">No Boundaries</a>" which was co-written by DioGuardi. This is the first season in which the winner failed to achieve gold album status.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_9">Season 9</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Season 9">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_9)" title="American Idol (season 9)">American Idol (season 9)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg/170px-Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg/255px-Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg/340px-Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lee-Dewyze-AI_Tour_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lee_DeWyze" title="Lee DeWyze">Lee DeWyze</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_9)" title="American Idol (season 9)">ninth season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The ninth season premiered on January 12, 2010. The upheaval at the judging panel continued. Ellen DeGeneres joined as a judge to replace Paula Abdul at the start of Hollywood Week.
</p><p>One of the most prominent auditioners this season was General <a href="/wiki/Larry_Platt" title="Larry Platt">Larry Platt</a> whose performance of "<a href="/wiki/Pants_on_the_Ground" title="Pants on the Ground">Pants on the Ground</a>" became a viral hit song.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Crystal_Bowersox" title="Crystal Bowersox">Crystal Bowersox</a>, who has <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus type 1">Type-I diabetes</a>, fell ill due to <a href="/wiki/Diabetic_ketoacidosis" title="Diabetic ketoacidosis">diabetic ketoacidosis</a> on the morning of the girls performance night for the top 20 week and was hospitalized.<sup id="cite_ref-crystal_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crystal-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The schedule was rearranged so the boys performed first and she could perform the following night instead; she later revealed that Ken Warwick, the show producer, wanted to disqualify her but she begged to be allowed to stay on the show.<sup id="cite_ref-crystal_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crystal-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Lynche" title="Michael Lynche">Michael Lynche</a> was the lowest vote getter at top nine and was given the Judges' Save. The next week <a href="/wiki/Katie_Stevens" title="Katie Stevens">Katie Stevens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Garcia" title="Andrew Garcia">Andrew Garcia</a> were eliminated. That week, Adam Lambert was invited back to be a mentor, the first <i>Idol</i> alum to do so. <i>Idol Gives Back</i> returned this season on April 21, 2010, and raised $45 million.<sup id="cite_ref-idol_gives_back_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idol_gives_back-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A special tribute to Simon Cowell was presented in the finale for his final season with the show. Many figures from the show's past, including Paula Abdul, made an appearance.
</p><p>The final two contestants were <a href="/wiki/Lee_DeWyze" title="Lee DeWyze">Lee DeWyze</a> and Bowersox. DeWyze was declared the winner during the May 26 finale. No new song was used as coronation song this year; instead, the two finalists each released a cover song – DeWyze chose <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Day" title="Beautiful Day">Beautiful Day</a>", and Bowersox chose <a href="/wiki/Patty_Griffin" title="Patty Griffin">Patty Griffin</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Up_to_the_Mountain_(MLK_Song)" title="Up to the Mountain (MLK Song)">Up to the Mountain</a>". This is the first season where neither finalist achieved significant album sales.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_10">Season 10</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Season 10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">American Idol (season 10)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg/170px-Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg/255px-Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg/340px-Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="517" data-file-height="671" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scotty_McCreery_May_14_2011_CROPPED2.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Scotty_McCreery" title="Scotty McCreery">Scotty McCreery</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">tenth season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The tenth season of the series premiered on January 19, 2011. Many changes were introduced this season, from the format to the personnel of the show. Jennifer Lopez and Steven Tyler joined Randy Jackson as judges following the departures of Simon Cowell (who left to launch the U.S. version of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S.)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (U.S.)">The X Factor</a></i>), Kara DioGuardi (whose contract was not renewed) and Ellen DeGeneres,<sup id="cite_ref-newjudges_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newjudges-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Lythgoe" title="Nigel Lythgoe">Nigel Lythgoe</a> returned as executive producer. <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Iovine" title="Jimmy Iovine">Jimmy Iovine</a>, chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Geffen_A%26M" class="mw-redirect" title="Interscope Geffen A&amp;M">Interscope Geffen A&amp;M</a> label group, the new partner of <i>American Idol</i>, acted as the in-house mentor in place of weekly guest mentors,<sup id="cite_ref-newjudges_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newjudges-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> although in later episodes special guest mentors such as <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> were brought in.
</p><p>The tenth season is the first to include online auditions where contestants could submit a 40-second video audition via Myspace.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karen_Rodriguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Karen Rodriguez">Karen Rodriguez</a> was one such auditioner and reached the final rounds.
</p><p>One of the more prominent contestants this year was <a href="/wiki/Chris_Medina" title="Chris Medina">Chris Medina</a>, whose story of caring for his brain-damaged fiancée received widespread coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Medina was cut in the Top 40 round. <a href="/wiki/Casey_Abrams" title="Casey Abrams">Casey Abrams</a>, who suffers from <a href="/wiki/Ulcerative_colitis" title="Ulcerative colitis">ulcerative colitis</a>, was hospitalized twice and missed the Top 13 result show. The judges used their one save on Abrams on the Top 11, and as a result this was the first season that 11 finalists went on tour instead of 10. In the following week, <a href="/wiki/Naima_Adedapo" title="Naima Adedapo">Naima Adedapo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thia_Megia" title="Thia Megia">Thia Megia</a> were both eliminated the following week.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pia_Toscano" title="Pia Toscano">Pia Toscano</a>, one of the presumed favorites to advance far in the season, was unexpectedly eliminated on April 7, 2011, finishing in ninth place. Her elimination drew criticisms from some former <i>Idol</i> contestants, as well as actor <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The two finalists in 2011 were <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Alaina" title="Lauren Alaina">Lauren Alaina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotty_McCreery" title="Scotty McCreery">Scotty McCreery</a>, both teenage country singers. McCreery won the competition on May 25, being the youngest male winner and the fourth male in a row to win <i>American Idol</i>. McCreery released his first single, "<a href="/wiki/I_Love_You_This_Big" title="I Love You This Big">I Love You This Big</a>", as his coronation song, and Alaina released "<a href="/wiki/Like_My_Mother_Does" title="Like My Mother Does">Like My Mother Does</a>". McCreery's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Clear_as_Day" title="Clear as Day">Clear as Day</a></i>, became the first debut album by an <i>Idol</i> winner to reach No. 1 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> since <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Studdard" title="Ruben Studdard">Ruben Studdard</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Soulful_(Ruben_Studdard_album)" title="Soulful (Ruben Studdard album)">Soulful</a></i> in 2003, and he became the youngest male artist to reach No. 1 on the Billboard 200.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_11">Season 11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Season 11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_11)" title="American Idol (season 11)">American Idol (season 11)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live!_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena,_July_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg/170px-Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg/255px-Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg/340px-Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live%21_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena%2C_July_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="380" data-file-height="564" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phillip_Phillips_at_the_American_Idols_Live!_Tour_2012_at_Seattle_Center%27s_Key_Arena,_July_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Phillip_Phillips" title="Phillip Phillips">Phillip Phillips</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_11)" title="American Idol (season 11)">eleventh season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The eleventh season premiered on January 18, 2012. One more finalist would join the Top 24 making it the Top 25, and that was <a href="/wiki/Jermaine_Jones_(singer)" title="Jermaine Jones (singer)">Jermaine Jones</a>. However, on March 14, Jones was disqualified in 12th place for concealing arrests and outstanding warrants. Jones denied the accusation that he concealed his arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Finalist <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Phillips" title="Phillip Phillips">Phillip Phillips</a> suffered from kidney pain and was taken to the hospital before the Top 13 results show, and later received medical procedure to alleviate a blockage caused by kidney stones.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> He was reported to have eight surgeries during his Idol run, and had considered quitting the show due to the pain.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He underwent surgery to remove the stones and reconstruct his kidney soon after the season had finished.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jessica_Sanchez" title="Jessica Sanchez">Jessica Sanchez</a> received the fewest votes during the Top 7 week, and the judges decided to use their "save" option on her, making her the first female recipient of the save. The following week, unlike previous seasons, <a href="/wiki/Colton_Dixon" title="Colton Dixon">Colton Dixon</a> was the only contestant sent home. Sanchez later made the final two, the first season where a recipient of the save reached the finale.
</p><p>Phillips became the winner, beating Sanchez. Fifth season finalist <a href="/wiki/Ace_Young" title="Ace Young">Ace Young</a> proposed marriage to third season runner-up <a href="/wiki/Diana_DeGarmo" title="Diana DeGarmo">Diana DeGarmo</a> on stage – which she accepted.
</p><p>Phillips released "<a href="/wiki/Home_(Phillip_Phillips_song)" title="Home (Phillip Phillips song)">Home</a>" as his coronation song, while Sanchez released "<a href="/wiki/Change_Nothing_(song)" title="Change Nothing (song)">Change Nothing</a>". Phillips' "Home" has since become the best selling of all coronation songs.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_12">Season 12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Season 12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_12)" title="American Idol (season 12)">American Idol (season 12)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Candice_Glover_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Candice_Glover_2013.jpg/170px-Candice_Glover_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Candice_Glover_2013.jpg/255px-Candice_Glover_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Candice_Glover_2013.jpg/340px-Candice_Glover_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="342" data-file-height="510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Candice_Glover_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Candice_Glover" title="Candice Glover">Candice Glover</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_12)" title="American Idol (season 12)">twelfth season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The twelfth season premiered on January 16, 2013. Judges Jennifer Lopez and Steven Tyler left the show after two seasons. This season's judging panel consisted of Randy Jackson, along with Mariah Carey, Keith Urban and Nicki Minaj. This was the first season since the ninth season to have four judges on the panel. The pre-season buzz and the early episodes of the show were dominated by the feud between the judges Minaj and Carey after a video of their dispute was leaked to <a href="/wiki/TMZ_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="TMZ (website)">TMZ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The top 10 contestants started with five males and five females, however, the males were eliminated consecutively in the first five weeks, with <a href="/wiki/Lazaro_Arbos" title="Lazaro Arbos">Lazaro Arbos</a> the last male to be eliminated. For the first time in the show's history, the top 5 contestants were all female. It was also the first time that the judges' "save" was not used, the top four contestants were therefore given an extra week to perform again with their votes carried over with no elimination in the first week.
</p><p>23-year-old <a href="/wiki/Candice_Glover" title="Candice Glover">Candice Glover</a> won the season with <a href="/wiki/Kree_Harrison" title="Kree Harrison">Kree Harrison</a> taking the runner-up spot. Glover is the first female to win <i>American Idol</i> since <a href="/wiki/Jordin_Sparks" title="Jordin Sparks">Jordin Sparks</a>. Glover released "<a href="/wiki/I_Am_Beautiful" title="I Am Beautiful">I Am Beautiful</a>" as a single while Harrison released "<a href="/wiki/All_Cried_Out_(Kree_Harrison_song)" title="All Cried Out (Kree Harrison song)">All Cried Out</a>" immediately after the show. Glover sold poorly with her debut album, and this is also the first season that the runner-up was not signed by a music label.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Towards the end of the season, Randy Jackson, the last remaining of the original judges, would no longer serve as a judge to pursue other business ventures.<sup id="cite_ref-I&#39;m_Leaving_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I&#39;m_Leaving-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Both judges Mariah Carey and Nicki Minaj also decided to leave after one season to focus on their music careers.<sup id="cite_ref-carey_minaj_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carey_minaj-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_13">Season 13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Season 13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_13)" title="American Idol (season 13)">American Idol (season 13)</a></div>
<p>The thirteenth season premiered on January 15, 2014. Randy Jackson and Keith Urban returned, though Jackson moved from the judging panel to the role of in-mentor. Mariah Carey and Nicki Minaj left the panel after one season. Former judge <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> and former mentor Harry Connick, Jr. joined Urban on the panel. Also, <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Lythgoe" title="Nigel Lythgoe">Nigel Lythgoe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Warwick" title="Ken Warwick">Ken Warwick</a> were replaced as executive producers by Per Blankens, Jesse Ignjatovic and Evan Pragger. Bill DeRonde replaced Warwick as a director of the audition episodes, while Louis J. Horvitz replaced Gregg Gelfand as a director of the show.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This was the first season where the contestants were permitted to perform in the final rounds songs they wrote themselves. In the Top 8, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Woolf" title="Sam Woolf">Sam Woolf</a> received the fewest votes, but he was saved from elimination by the judges. The 500th episode of the series was the Top 3 performance night.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Caleb_Johnson" title="Caleb Johnson">Caleb Johnson</a> was named the winner of the season, with <a href="/wiki/Jena_Irene" class="mw-redirect" title="Jena Irene">Jena Irene</a> as the runner-up.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>  Johnson released "<a href="/wiki/As_Long_as_You_Love_Me_(Caleb_Johnson_song)" title="As Long as You Love Me (Caleb Johnson song)">As Long as You Love Me</a>" as his coronation single while Irene released "We Are One".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_14">Season 14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Season 14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_14)" title="American Idol (season 14)">American Idol (season 14)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg/170px-Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg/255px-Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg/340px-Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1933" data-file-height="2479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nick_Fradiani_at_the_National_Memorial_Day_Concert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nick_Fradiani" title="Nick Fradiani">Nick Fradiani</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_14)" title="American Idol (season 14)">fourteenth</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p>The fourteenth season premiered on January 7, 2015. Jennifer Lopez, Keith Urban and Harry Connick, Jr. returned for their respective fourth, third and second seasons as judges. Eighth season runner-up <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">Adam Lambert</a> filled in for Urban during the New York City auditions. Randy Jackson did not return as the in-house mentor for this season.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Borchetta" title="Scott Borchetta">Scott Borchetta</a> replaced Jackson as the mentor.
</p><p>Changes this season include only airing one episode a week during the final ten.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Coca-Cola ended their longtime sponsorship of the show<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> and Ford Motor Company maintained a reduced role. The winner of the season also received a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Big_Machine_Records" title="Big Machine Records">Big Machine Records</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nick_Fradiani" title="Nick Fradiani">Nick Fradiani</a> won the season, defeating <a href="/wiki/Clark_Beckham" title="Clark Beckham">Clark Beckham</a>. By winning, Fradiani became the first winner from the Northeast region. Fradiani released "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Life_(Nick_Fradiani_song)" title="Beautiful Life (Nick Fradiani song)">Beautiful Life</a>" as his coronation single while Beckham released "Champion". <a href="/wiki/Jax_(singer)" title="Jax (singer)">Jax</a>, the third place finalist, also released a single called "Forcefield".
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_15">Season 15</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Season 15">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_15)" title="American Idol (season 15)">American Idol (season 15)</a></div>
<p>Fox announced on May 11, 2015 that the fifteenth season would be the final season of <i>American Idol</i>; as such, the season was expected to have an additional focus on the program's alumni. Ryan Seacrest returned as host, with Harry Connick Jr., Keith Urban, and Jennifer Lopez all returning as judges.<sup id="cite_ref-Idol_Cancellation_(May_2015)_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Idol_Cancellation_(May_2015)-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The season was shortened by four weeks compared to previous years.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> During the finale episode, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> praised the millions of young people that voted for contestants and pitched that they vote in the upcoming <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">election</a>. The farewell season concluded on April 7, 2016. Seacrest signed off by saying: "And one more time—this is so tough—we say to you from Hollywood, goodnight America", and then he added, "for now."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trent_Harmon" title="Trent Harmon">Trent Harmon</a> won the season against runner-up <a href="/wiki/La%27Porsha_Renae" title="La&#39;Porsha Renae">La'Porsha Renae</a>. Harmon released "<a href="/wiki/Falling_(Trent_Harmon_song)" title="Falling (Trent Harmon song)">Falling</a>" co-written by Keith Urban as his coronation song.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Renae's "<a href="/wiki/Battles_(La%27Porsha_Renae_song)" title="Battles (La&#39;Porsha Renae song)">Battles</a>", third-place finisher <a href="/wiki/Dalton_Rapattoni" title="Dalton Rapattoni">Dalton Rapattoni</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Strike_A_Match" class="mw-redirect" title="Strike A Match">Strike A Match</a>" and fourth-place finisher <a href="/wiki/MacKenzie_Bourg" title="MacKenzie Bourg">MacKenzie Bourg</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Roses_(MacKenzie_Bourg_song)" title="Roses (MacKenzie Bourg song)">Roses</a>" were also released as singles.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.93present:_ABC_revival"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–present:_ABC_revival">2018–present: ABC revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 2018–present: ABC revival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In early 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> reported that Fremantle Media was in talks to revive the show for <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> or for its original network, Fox.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> A dispute between Fremantle and Core Media Group derailed these plans.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In May 2017, ABC was making a bid to revive the program.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> ABC acquired the rights to the series, and <i>American Idol</i> returned for the 2017–18 television season.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_16">Season 16</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Season 16">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_16)" title="American Idol (season 16)">American Idol (season 16)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maddie_Poppe,_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg/170px-Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="333" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg/255px-Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c7/Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg/340px-Maddie_Poppe%2C_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maddie_Poppe,_winner_of_American_Idol_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maddie_Poppe" title="Maddie Poppe">Maddie Poppe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_16)" title="American Idol (season 16)">sixteenth season</a> winner</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_1_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_1-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Luke_Bryan" title="Luke Bryan">Luke Bryan</a><sup id="cite_ref-Bryan_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bryan-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">Lionel Richie</a><sup id="cite_ref-Richie_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richie-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> were the three judges and Ryan Seacrest returned as host.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The sixthteen season premiered on March 11, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The season was again shortened compared to the previous season to twelve weeks, with multiple elimination in the final rounds. On May 21, 2018 the season concluded, crowning <a href="/wiki/Maddie_Poppe" title="Maddie Poppe">Maddie Poppe</a> winner and <a href="/wiki/Caleb_Lee_Hutchinson" title="Caleb Lee Hutchinson">Caleb Lee Hutchinson</a> runner-up.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_17">Season 17</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Season 17">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_17)" title="American Idol (season 17)">American Idol (season 17)</a></div>
<p>ABC renewed the revival series for another season. Perry, Bryan and Richie returned as judges, while Seacrest returned as host.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The seventeen season permiered on March 3, 2019. For the finale, the show no longer features separate performance and result shows. On May 19, 2019 the season concluded, crowning <a href="/wiki/Laine_Hardy" title="Laine Hardy">Laine Hardy</a> winner and <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Aranda" title="Alejandro Aranda">Alejandro Aranda</a> runner-up. Hardy released a single, "<a href="/wiki/Flame_(Laine_Hardy_song)" title="Flame (Laine Hardy song)">Flame</a>", immediately after the win, but Aranda did not. However, Aranda did announce he would release a new single and a new album in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_18">Season 18</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Season 18">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_18)" title="American Idol (season 18)">American Idol (season 18)</a></div>
<p>On May 13, 2019, the series was renewed for an eighteenth season and will premiere in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Season_18_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Season_18-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Ryan Seacrest will return as the host.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._television_ratings">U.S. television ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=American_Idol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: U.S. television ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seasonal rankings (based on average total viewers per episode) of <i>American Idol</i>. It holds the distinction of having the longest winning streak in the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_ratings" title="Nielsen ratings">Nielsen annual television ratings</a>; it became the highest-rated of all television programs in the United States overall for an unprecedented seven consecutive years,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> or eight consecutive (and total) years when either its performance or result show was ranked number one overall.<sup id="cite_ref-ratings_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ratings-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><i>Each U.S. network television season starts in late September and ends in late May, which coincides with the completion of May <a href="/wiki/Sweeps" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweeps">sweeps</a>.</i></dd></dl>
